data-stale="false" width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p><strong>Processing file:</strong> 07_Unit_Five_Gynaecology.pdf</p></div></div></div><div class="stElementContainer element-container st-emotion-cache-kj6hex eu6p4el1" data-testid="stElementContainer" data-stale="false" width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p>UNIT FIVE: GYNAECOLOGY</p>
<p>Gynaecology refers to diseases or conditions peculiar to women's reproductive systems. Patients with gynaecological disorders require a lot of understanding because of the emotional and the physical considerations that govern the situation. You should always respect the confidentiality of the patient's problems and share any information obtained only with those directly involved professionally with the care of the patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-objectives">Unit Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain gynaecological investigations for patients with reproductive disorders</li>
<li>Describe menstrual disorders and provide appropriate care</li>
<li>Describe bleeding disorders in early pregnancy and take appropriate action</li>
<li>Describe the appropriate management of genital disorders and injuries</li>
<li>Describe the management of infertility and climacteric crisis</li>
<li>Describe neoplastic conditions and take appropriate action</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-1-gynaecological-investigations">SECTION 1: GYNAECOLOGICAL INVESTIGATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-1-gynaecological-investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Just like any other aspect of medicine, gynaecology and obstetrics require some investigative work. As a health worker, you must find clues in the patient's history and physical examination to help you make the right diagnosis. The more thorough the history and physical examination, the better the chances of making an accurate diagnosis.</p>
<p>You may also need to carry out certain tests and investigations in order to come to the correct conclusion. However, in order to take a complete history and conduct a thorough investigation, you need to know what in particular you are looking for.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section, you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Describe history taking</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>List various tests and gynaecological radiographic diagnostic procedures</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="gynaecological-history">Gynaecological History<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gynaecological-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>History taking should place an emphasis on the gynaecological history of the patient. This does not mean that other histories should be ignored. For the sake of minimising repetition, you will not go through the whole process. When taking a gynaecological history, you should enquire into the following:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="menstruation">Menstruation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#menstruation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Menstruation, including the age at which she had her first menstrual period, that is, menarche equivalent to 'K', the length of the menstrual cycle, duration of the periods and the amount of blood loss and regularity as well as the date of the Last Normal Menstrual Period (LNMP).</p>
<p>Always record this information as 'K 13 5/28 regular'. This means that the periods began at the age of 13, last for five days and occur every 28 days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="gynaecological-operations">Gynaecological Operations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gynaecological-operations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Take the history of any gynaecological operations, including the dates of operations. Possible gynaecological operations include dilatation and curettage, evacuation, laparotomy and hysterectomy and post-operative outcomes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="contraceptive-history">Contraceptive History<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contraceptive-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Take the patient's contraceptive history, especially on surgical contraceptions, including the type of contraceptive, duration of use, side effects and when she stopped using it.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="sexual-behaviour">Sexual Behaviour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sexual-behaviour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Ask about the patient's sexual behaviour, noting that questions should be non-judgemental and you should not embarrass the patient. You should find out whether she is sexually active, whether the relationship is satisfactory and, if not, why. For example, find out if she has painful or difficult sex referred to as dyspareunia. In case of infertility find out also whether intercourse is normal, frequent and what time in the cycle. You need to ask if there is any post-coital bleeding or not. This information may well help you to detect any sexually transmitted diseases.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 235 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 236 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lifestyle-habits">Lifestyle Habits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lifestyle-habits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Ask if she smokes or takes alcohol.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary">Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should make a summary of the history you have taken by picking out the important positive and negative information obtained. This will guide you when performing a physical examination.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physical-examination">Physical Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A physical examination should be made up of a general, abdominal and vaginal examination. Abdominal and vaginal examinations were covered in module one, unit two, section three, so for now you will only look at general examination in detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-examination">General Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A general examination provides more information about a patient and also gives the clinician a chance to establish a rapport with the patient. General examination usually includes a check on the vital signs and the general condition of the patient. When you are doing a general examination, you should look for the development of secondary sexual characteristics, including breast development (palpate for masses) and body hair distribution, especially the pubic hair. Hair on the chest and chin in a female will mean that she has more androgens.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>Antiseptic is not used in this procedure because a specimen may be taken. If antiseptic is used to clean the vulva, it will destroy organisms hence leading to a false result.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gynaecological-tests">Gynaecological Tests<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gynaecological-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As mentioned earlier, there are a number of laboratory tests and radiological investigations that you can carry out, in order to reach a definitive diagnosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="urine">Urine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#urine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Urinalysis should be carried out to check the appearance of the urine, including colour and foam, chemical content such as protein and glucose, and micro-organisms such as bacteria and parasites.</p>
<p>A pregnancy test, if indicated, may be performed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="blood">Blood<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#blood" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Blood should be tested for haemoglobin levels (Hb) or full haemogram, Widal test and brucellosis test and also for VDRL (syphilis).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vagina-and-cervix">Vagina and Cervix<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vagina-and-cervix" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Urethral smears and pus swabs should be taken to test for neisseria gonorrhoea. Take a high vaginal swabs test for candida albicans, trichomonas vaginalis, and neisseria gonorrhoea. You should also perform a cytological test for cancer as well as a cervical biopsy for further histological assessment, which will be covered later in this unit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cytological-test-papanicolao-test-pap-smear">Cytological Test/Papanicolao Test (Pap Smear)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cytological-test-papanicolao-test-pap-smear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a test that should be carried out on women of reproductive age once every year. Cancer of the cervix is one of the leading causes of mortality among women worldwide.</p>
<p>This test reveals the cancer in its early stages when it can be managed effectively.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cervical-biopsy">Cervical Biopsy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cervical-biopsy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This test can also detect problems on the cervix. It may be done as an office procedure without anaesthesia, whereby the lesion is visualised by a colposcope and one or more punch biopsies. A colposcopy is a binocular inspection of the cervix with a magnification of up to 20 times.</p>
<p>The patient is advised to rest for 24 hours after a biopsy and to leave the packing or tampon in place for the recommended time, usually 8 to 24 hours. Vital signs should be frequently checked and any excess bleeding reported. Sexual intercourse should be delayed until the physician indicates that it is permissible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="endoscopic-examination">Endoscopic Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endoscopic-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This examination involves entering the body organs by use of a scope. A scope is a special tubular instrument with a light attached to the end. When introduced into the hollow organs of the body they can be seen and studied. There are various types of endoscopic examinations.</p>
<p>The pelvic endoscopy/culdoscopy involves the use of a culdoscope, which is a tubular, lighted instrument similar to a cystoscope or laparoscope. An incision is made in the posterior</p>
<p>vaginal</p>
<p>cul-de-sac (fornix) to admit the instrument. It is commonly used to detect any pelvic masses. The patient is prepared as for vaginal operation and may be under local anaesthesia. The procedure is conducted in the operating room, with the patient in a knee-chest position.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="laparoscopy">Laparoscopy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#laparoscopy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Indications are similar to that of a culdoscopy. However, with laparoscopy, it is also possible to perform minor operative procedures like tubal ligation, ovarian biopsy and lysis of peritubal adhesion.</p>
<p>During this examination, a scope (of about 10mm diameter) is inserted into the peritoneal cavity through a two centimetre sub-umbilical incision to allow visualisation of the pelvic structure. Dilatation and curettage follows, to position a surgical instrument, which permits manipulation of the uterus during the laparoscopy, thus affording better visualisation.</p>
<p>The coldlight endoscope is passed through the cannula and the inspection made. An assistant or the operator himself can move the uterus about by means of the forceps on the cervix and a dilator or Spackman's cannula in the uterus. A camera attached to the eyepiece of the laparoscope permits assistants and observers to share the surgeon's view on a video screen and permits video recording of the findings or procedure.</p>
<p>Drapes are used during this procedure, but have been omitted in the illustration to allow unobstructed view.</p>
<p>Special biopsy forceps can be passed through another cannula and used to lift up any tissue that may be obstructing the view or to take ovarian biopsies. Some adhesions may be divided using laparoscopy scissors. Many procedures are now performed entirely or assisted by laparoscopy.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-17d639f8.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<p>A better view of the pelvis, lower abdomen and visceral contents is also facilitated by injection of a prescribed amount of CO₂ intraperitoneally into the cavity (insufflation). This separates the intestine from the pelvic organs.</p>
<p>The procedure is performed under general anaesthesia, meaning patients have to be prepared preoperatively. The patient is carefully observed for several hours to detect any complications, for example, bleeding or burns from the coagulator. The observation includes monitoring vital signs and signs of per vaginal bleeding. Reassure the patient and discharge when the vital signs become stable.</p>
<p>Next, move on to look at another procedure, which involves entering into the uterine cavity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hysteroscopy">Hysteroscopy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hysteroscopy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This procedure is indicated as a diagnostic measure only in complex situations, for example, infertility, unexplained bleeding and retained Intrauterine Device (IUD).</p>
<p>The hysteroscope is used to visualise all the parts of the uterine cavity. This procedure is best performed about five days after completion of menstruation (estrogenic phase of the menstrual cycle). This is because the fresh/new cells lining the uterine cavity can be studied properly in order to give accurate findings.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>Hysteroscopy is contraindicated in patients with cervical or endometrial carcinoma due to dissemination of cancer cells.</p>
<p>Next move on to look at radiographic diagnostic procedures. It is important for you to know them so that you can provide appropriate care and advice to the patient undergoing these tests.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 237 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Many radiological procedures, for example, x-ray films, barium enemas and intravenous urography, are helpful in the diagnosis of pelvic conditions. A few of the procedures specifically related to the diagnosis of gynaecological disorders will be covered here.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hysterosalpingogram-uterotubogram">Hysterosalpingogram (Uterotubogram)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hysterosalpingogram-uterotubogram" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an x-ray study of the uterus and uterine tubes after injection of a contrast medium. This is done to study sterility problems, tubal patency and/or the presence of pathological conditions in the uterine cavity.</p>
<p>A patient undergoing this examination should have her intestines evacuated by enema. 'Starve' the patient for at least four to six hours. Give analgesic for comfort since some patients may experience nausea, vomiting, cramps and faintness. Briefly explain the procedure to the patient and give reassurance. Observe the vital signs.</p>
<p>The patient may feel some discomfort after the procedure. You should continue observing her vital signs and if the patient is not nauseated, give her food as soon as she can tolerate it. You should also provide plenty of fluids to flush the urinary system.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="computerised-tomography-ct-scanning">Computerised Tomography (CT Scanning)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#computerised-tomography-ct-scanning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A CT scan can reveal the presence of cancer and its extension into the retroperitoneal lymph nodes and skeletal involvement.</p>
<p>The CT scan has several advantages over an ultrasound and it is more effective, especially with obese patients and/or patients with a distended bowel or stomach. This is because it penetrates deep into the organ targeted and reveals more information about these organs. In preparation, the patient should be 'starved' before this procedure.</p>
<p>The scanner takes repeated x-ray pictures of a cross-section of the body (nearly 300 pictures within five seconds) as the x-ray tube is rotated around the patient.</p>
<p>Some absorption of x-rays takes place according to the density of the tissues through which the x-rays pass. Thus the difference between the amount of radiation entering the body and amount measured by the detectors is equivalent to the density of the tissues.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ultrasound">Ultrasound<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ultrasound" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is commonly used and does not require any special preparation of the patient, except to ensure that they have a full bladder. This is because a distended bladder usually pushes the uterus out of the pelvic cavity allowing it to be properly viewed. It is used to diagnose pelvic tumours and other abnormalities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-2-menstrual-disorders">SECTION 2: MENSTRUAL DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-2-menstrual-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In this section you are going to focus on menstrual disorders. Menstruation is a normal body event in every woman, even though for some it may be an uncomfortable experience. On a light note, however, there is an old adage that says 'the menstrual flow is the tears of a disappointed uterus'.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section, you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe factors that influence menstruation</li>
<li>Describe the various menstrual disorders and their management</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="factors-influencing-normal-menstruation">Factors Influencing Normal Menstruation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-influencing-normal-menstruation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The events occurring in the following organs influence the mechanism of normal menstruation:</p>
<ul>
<li>The hypothalamus influences the anterior pituitary gland to produce follicle stimulating hormone.</li>
<li>The anterior pituitary gland produces follicle stimulating hormone, which matures the Graafian follicle under the influence of the hypothalamus. It also produces the luteinising hormone, which influences the development of corpus luteum to produce oestrogen or progesterone.</li>
<li>The ovaries develop the Graafian follicle.</li>
<li>The uterine endometrium thickens under the influence of oestrogen and progesterone, in preparation to receive the ovum.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="menstrual-disorders">Menstrual Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#menstrual-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h4 level="4" id="amenorrhoea">Amenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#amenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h4></div>
<p>Amenorrhoea is a symptom, not a disease. It is derived from the Greek word amenrein, which translates as follows:</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>A... without
Men... month</p>
<ul>
<li>Rein... to flow</li>
</ul>
<p>It can, therefore, be interpreted to mean 'without monthly flow', thus amenorrhoea means 'absence or cessation of menstruation'. The absence of menstrual periods can be physiologically normal.</p>
<p>Move on to find out at which point amenorrhoea is considered to be normal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="name-at-least-three-periods-in-a-woman-s-life-when-amenorrhoea-is-considered-normal">Name at least three periods in a woman's life when amenorrhoea is considered normal.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#name-at-least-three-periods-in-a-woman-s-life-when-amenorrhoea-is-considered-normal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Your answer should include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Before puberty, when the hormones concerned have not started functioning.</li>
<li>During pregnancy, when the hormones concerned are diverted to the growth of the fertilised ovum.</li>
<li>During lactation (after delivery), which results in lactation amenorrhoea due to the presence of prolactin.</li>
<li>At menopause, when the hormones diminish and cease to be produced.</li>
</ul>
<p>You have focused on pathological amenorrhoea, which can be divided into two, namely primary and secondary amenorrhoea.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="primary-amenorrhoea">Primary Amenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-amenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Primary amenorrhoea means that menstruation has never occurred. This is seen in a young woman who is over 17 years of age and who has not yet begun to menstruate but exhibits signs of sexual maturation. Pathological primary amenorrhoea is when the patient has never menstruated and has not developed secondary sexual characteristics.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="primary-amenorrhoea">Primary Amenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-amenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are two main factors that lead to primary amenorrhoea. These are hormonal factors and developmental anomalies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hormonal-factors">Hormonal Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormonal-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is due to the malfunctioning of the pituitary gland. As a result, the hormones responsible for sex maturation are affected, which in turn affects the beginning of menstruation.</p>
<p>In Cushing's syndrome, the excessive production of cortisols may hinder menstruation from starting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="developmental-anomalies">Developmental Anomalies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#developmental-anomalies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During the development of the foetus, the vagina, uterus or ovaries may fail to develop. The congenital abnormality in the vagina that causes primary amenorrhoea is an imperforate hymen. In this case, the girl experiences all the feelings and discomforts of menstrual flow. There is actually menstruation and the blood accumulates behind the hymen, (in the vagina), but does not come out. This condition is known as cryptomenorrhoea and when not treated, the uterus distends, leading to what is known as haematometra. The girl may present with abdominal pain and the absence of menstruation. The condition can be cured by an incision of the hymen to allow the blood to flow out freely. After the incision you should advise the girl to maintain high standards of hygiene. The vulva should be cleaned three times a day until healed.</p>
<p>Other causes include male pseudohermaphroditism (a male develops as a female) and Turner's syndrome where one has only one x-chromosome. Now move on to look at secondary amenorrhoea.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="secondary-amenorrhoea">Secondary Amenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secondary-amenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Secondary amenorrhoea simply means that the periods, which were once present, have stopped.</p>
<p>There are some women who have a longer cycle of up to two to three months and this is considered normal as long as it is regular. However, secondary amenorrhoea occurs after a normal menarche, which then ceases for more than six months. Six months is a considerable duration for it to be abnormal.</p>
<p>Now move on to look at some of the possible causes of secondary amenorrhoea.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hormonal-disturbances">Hormonal Disturbances<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormonal-disturbances" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hormonal disturbances in the pituitary gland can lead to hypopituitarism, especially after severe postpartum haemorrhage and collapse. This leads to pituitary cachexia/Sheehan's disease. In this condition, there is temporary deprivation of blood supply to the pituitary, leading to ischaemia. This impairs the functions of the pituitary gland.</p>
<p>In addition, disturbances in the adrenal gland, thyroid gland and/or ovaries can affect the influence of the hypothalamus on the pituitary gland.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 239 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 240 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="debilitating-systemic-disorders">Debilitating Systemic Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#debilitating-systemic-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Chronic diseases that cause general ill health, for example, genital tuberculosis, or severe anaemia may lead to secondary amenorrhoea.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nervous-disorders">Nervous Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nervous-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Any stress can act on the hypothalamus to inhibit follicle stimulating hormone/leutinising hormone-releasing hormone.</p>
<p>This may lead to stress or hypothalamic amenorrhoea. Minor emotional upsets related to being away from home, attending college, tension from schoolwork or interpersonal problems are the most common causes of secondary amenorrhoea, especially in adolescents.</p>
<p>Other related disorders that cause stress include longstanding psychiatric disorders, especially depression or anxiety and stress due to exercise, which leads to exercise amenorrhoea. This is especially common in marathon runners. Others include brain tumours which may destroy the hypothalamus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drugs">Drugs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Contraceptives may lead to post contraceptive amenorrhoea and in some individuals it may take three to six months before the return of menstruation. This is because the ovulation had been suppressed and therefore had an effect on the hormones concerned.</p>
<p>Phenothiazines, especially in large doses, may lead to amenorrhoea due to prolactinaemia and certain hypotensive agents have also been implicated. You may remember (as mentioned in lactation amenorrhoea) that these drugs stimulate prolactin.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dietary-amenorrhoea">Dietary Amenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dietary-amenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Loss of weight due to prolonged fasting will affect the hypothalamic function in ways which are not yet understood. Nutritional deficiency will also affect menstruation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ovarian-cysts">Ovarian Cysts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ovarian-cysts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Ovarian cysts, especially follicular and corpus luteum cysts, cause amenorrhoea, however these tend to regress with time and menstruation resumes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="oligomenorrhoea">Oligomenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#oligomenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Finally, this is a type of amenorrhoea where there is infrequent menstruation, which may occur months before menopause and, at times, due to emotional upset.</p>
<p>A woman with this problem should be investigated thoroughly to exclude other serious conditions, for example, neoplasms. You should reassure the patient if the cause of the condition is emotional.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-amenorrhoea">Management of Amenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-amenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>After discussing both types of amenorrhoea, you will now look at their management.</p>
<p>First, establish the cause of the condition. In each case you must take a detailed history and then carry out a clinical examination to rule out pregnancy.</p>
<p>You should also consider the general health of the woman, including psychological and environmental factors. In the case of a young girl who appears normal on examination, it is better to wait until she is 18 years old but in the meantime reassure her and give her health education on sexuality.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The most common cause of secondary amenorrhoea is almost always pregnancy, therefore, an obstetric and gynaecological history is important to making a diagnosis.</p>
<p>A series of investigations can be performed and these should include the following steps:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="history-taking">History Taking<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-taking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is very important as it helps you make a distinction between primary and secondary amenorrhoea and, therefore, institute appropriate management measures.</p>
<p>Some women have very infrequent and scanty bleeding, which is virtually primary amenorrhoea. If the patient is experiencing the physical disturbances of menstruation without actually bleeding, a cyclical change in the hormone level can be assumed and the cause of amenorrhoea is likely to be in the genital tract.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pelvic-examination">Pelvic Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pelvic-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is essential to exclude pregnancy or uterine hypoplasia (in virgins this is usually done under general anaesthesia).</p>
<p>A bi-manual examination can reveal gross abnormalities such as cryptomenorrhoea.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-19c9056c.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<p>Remember to inspect the secondary sexual characteristics during pelvic examination.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="radiological-examination">Radiological Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#radiological-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should take an x-ray of the chest and a straight skull
x-ray to detect enlargement of the sella turcica (pituitary fossa).</p>
<p>You will remember the pituitary gland plays a great role and chronic diseases like TB can affect menstruation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="endocrine-tests">Endocrine Tests<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endocrine-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To find out the hormonal factors, the following should be carried out:</p>
<ul>
<li>Collection of urine samples for over 24 hours to measure levels of different hormones.</li>
<li>Estimation of blood hormone levels. The hormones investigated are follicle stimulating, leutinising and prolactin. If there is hyper-prolactinaemia, then refer the patient to an endocrinologist for pituitary tumour investigation and management.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="laparoscopy">Laparoscopy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#laparoscopy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is done to detect any developmental anomalies.</p>
<p>An ovarian biopsy can also be carried out during this procedure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dilatation-and-curettage">Dilatation and Curettage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dilatation-and-curettage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is commonly performed, especially in countries where tuberculosis is common. The presence of the acid-fast bacilli in the endometrial cells or any other organisms may be the cause of amenorrhoea.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="others">Others<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#others" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>More recent technologies include the ultrasound or CT scan which detect various abnormalities. It can reveal the presence of tumours in the ovaries or the adrenal gland.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-amenorrhoea-medical-treatment">Management of Amenorrhoea - Medical Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-amenorrhoea-medical-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The medical treatment will depend on the cause of the amenorrhoea.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clomiphene-citrate-clomid">Clomiphene Citrate (Clomid)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clomiphene-citrate-clomid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If ovulation is the problem, then it can be induced using clomiphene citrate. This drug should be restricted to those individuals desiring pregnancy because it acts on the Graafian follicle. It can also be used in adolescents with recurrent ovulatory bleeding in an attempt to establish regular ovulatory cycles.</p>
<p>The dosage initially given is 50mg daily for five days and ovulation is expected to occur five to eleven days following discontinuation. If there is no response, the dose is gradually increased up to 200mg.</p>
<p>Side effects of clomid include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Hyper-stimulation leading to enlargement of the ovaries.</li>
<li>Multiple gestation because more than one ovum may mature.</li>
<li>Abortion is common with patients treated for infertility.</li>
<li>Teratology, that is, the increased incidence of congenital anomalies, if conception takes place while the woman is still taking the drug.</li>
<li>Bloating, nausea and vomiting.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="human-menopausal-gonadotrophin-hmg-and-human-chorionic-gonadotrophin-hcg-personal">Human Menopausal Gonadotrophin (HMG) and Human Chorionic Gonadotrophin (HCG) Personal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#human-menopausal-gonadotrophin-hmg-and-human-chorionic-gonadotrophin-hcg-personal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a preparation of leutinising hormone and follicle stimulating hormone extracted from human menopausal urine and is available in ratio of 1:1.</p>
<p>The therapy is indicated when there is failure to ovulate even after clomid administration for six to twelve months. The dosage is HMG 375 units daily, increasing progressively up to 1500 units daily.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Remember:
Hormonal monitoring during this therapy is important in order to keep the hormones in balance.</p>
<p>Bromocriptine
This is effective as an ovulatory agent in most patients with hyperprolactinaemia from an anaplastic source.
It acts by suppressing the central and peripheral concentrations of prolactin, so that its level stimulates the production of oestrogen and progesterone. The dosage initially is 2.5mg up to four weeks.</p>
<p>Other Agents
Other agents used for the induction of ovulation include glucocorticosteroids (dexamethasone 0.5mg nocte, prednisone 0.75mg) and oestradiol (estrogen).
Do not forget that emotional disturbance is one of the features that cause amenorrhoea. Such patients will require psychotherapy to relieve the tension/stress. Through history taking, you may be able to get clues to any emotional stress and try to allay the patient's anxiety.</p>
<p>Surgical Management
Pituitary tumours may require excision.
Now move on to look at the other group of menstrual disorders.</p>
<p>Dysmenorrhoea
Dysmenorrhoea means painful menstruation. Some women experience pain and discomfort during menstruation and many will learn to live with it. However, in some women the pain is severe enough to make the woman seek treatment.
There are two types of dysmenorrhoea:</p>
<ul>
<li>Primary Dysmenorrhoea (also known at Spasmodic Dysmenorrhoea)</li>
<li>Secondary Dysmenorrhoea (also known as Congestive Dysmenorrhoea)
Now move on to look at these in more detail.</li>
</ul>
<p>Primary (or Spasmodic) Dysmenorrhoea
You may have come across young girls seeking treatment due to abdominal pain during menstruation. This is a common complaint and usually starts soon after puberty, although the first few cycles may have been painless.
The pain starts at the beginning of the period and lasts from a few hours to two days. This pain is 'cramp-like' and is felt in the pelvic and lower back region, and may radiate into the legs. Severe pain is sometimes accompanied by nausea, vomiting and fainting. These reactions may encourage the woman to seek treatment.
The causes of this condition are not well known but several theories have been put forward. It may probably be caused by ischaemia due to prolonged contraction of the uterine muscle occurring in the first day of menstruation. The ischaemia means that oxygen to the uterine muscle is cut off accounting for the pain. In this case, it is said that childbirth may cure this condition since after the uterus has held the baby, it is more vascular and so not easily ischaemic.
It has also been posited that dysmenorrhoeic uteri are hypoplastic but there is no evidence. Endocrine abnormalities have occasionally been implicated, probably due to the imbalances. Prostaglandins from disintegrating endometrium may cause uterine spasms (that is why in cases of dysmenorrhoea the concentration of PGF2 in menstrual fluids is increased).
Psychological factors undoubtedly aggravate symptoms, for example, there may be fear of sexual or reproductive abnormalities, leading the uterus to spasm.
Cervical stenosis also seems to be a factor. It is believed that during pregnancy and delivery the stenosed cervix is dilated hence the reason the problem may disappear after delivery.</p>
<p>Management of Primary Dysmenorrhoea
Unfortunately, a spontaneous cure does not occur soon enough for most women who suffer from primary dysmenorrhoea. Therefore, as part of your management, you should perform the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Take history with special reference to the severity and duration of the pain.</li>
<li>Perform a physical examination to exclude pelvic tumours.</li>
<li>Give a full and frank discussion of the normal cycle as this is an important part of treatment.</li>
<li>Share health messages on the importance of exercise and the avoidance of unnecessary restriction of general activities.</li>
<li>Provide women suffering from dysmenorrhoea with sympathy and support. Administer a suitable drug which will alleviate the pain sufficiently to allow a normal existence during the period time. Fortunately, patients tend to</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>improve or at least complain less as they grow older.</p>
<p>Drugs that can alleviate pain include any antipyretics and analgesics. These should be the most effective drugs to inhibit the synthesis of prostaglandin, that is, if the prostaglandin's theory is correct.</p>
<p>These include aspirin and paracetamol, which are widely used and usually prescribed as two tablets three times daily. Mefenamic acid (ponstan) 500mg three times daily is also common. This drug is said to prevent the action of prostaglandin on muscles as well as inhibit its production. Other drugs include flufenamic acid (arlef) and indomethacin (indocid).</p>
<p>Many of these drugs are usually prescribed for the relief of rheumatic pain but have been used with success in dysmenorrhoea.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>These drugs must be used carefully as they can adversely affect patients with other medical disorders, including asthma. Do not give strong analgesics like morphine, pethidine and other addictive drugs.</p>
<p>Another effective management method is the contraceptive pill. In a small number of girls, when simple measures fail, they can be put on the family planning pill which, by inhibiting ovulation, will result in painless periods. These few individuals should be placed on the pill for four to six months continuously, after which the problem may disappear completely. This is achieved with a high-progesterone, low-oestrogen combined pill, for example, minovular.</p>
<p>Surgery, in the form of pre-sacral neurectomy, may be offered as a last resort to a patient whose dysmenorrhoea cannot be relieved by any other means and is interfering with her daily life.</p>
<p>Now move on to look at secondary dysmenorrhoea.</p>
<p><strong>Secondary (or Congestive) Dysmenorrhoea</strong></p>
<p>This type of dysmenorrhoea may be caused by some pathology in the pelvis. The patient usually complains of a dull aching pain in the lower abdomen. The pain commonly begins three to four days (or sometimes up to ten days) prior to menstruation, and ceases after the flow is established or may persist throughout the period.</p>
<p>Pain is often made worse by exercise.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>Dysmenorrhoea, which starts after the age of 30 years should always be investigated since it could be due to some pathology in the reproductive system.</p>
<p>The causes of secondary dysmenorrhoea include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Chronic Pelvic Inflammatory Diseases (PID)</li>
<li>Endometriosis</li>
<li>Uterine fibroids</li>
<li>Abnormal fibrous attachments (adhesions)</li>
<li>Salpingitis</li>
</ul>
<p>These conditions and their management will be covered later in this unit and also in the next unit (unit six). It is important to remember, however, that in this country the most common cause of secondary dysmenorrhoea is chronic PID and also with most women complaining of infertility. Treatment of the cause will usually relieve the dysmenorrhoea, but as you know successful treatment of chronic PID is difficult and so prevention should be emphasised.</p>
<p><strong>Management of Secondary Dysmenorrhoea</strong></p>
<p>Take a full history to find out the cause of the condition, so that the patient can receive treatment according to the cause.</p>
<p>There are other symptoms, which may cause dysmenorrhoea and these will be discussed in the next sub-section.</p>
<p><strong>Pre Menstrual Tension Syndrome (PMT)</strong></p>
<p>This condition is due to a large group of symptoms, which appear regularly and predictably about 12 days before the onset of menstruation. This group of symptoms includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Water retention leading to weight gain, painful breasts, abdominal distension and feeling of bloatedness.</li>
<li>Pain in the form of backache, headache, tiredness and muscle stiffness.</li>
<li>Autonomic reaction, for instance, dizziness/faintness, cold sweats, nausea and vomiting and hot flushes.</li>
<li>Mood change, including tension, irritability, depression and crying spells.</li>
<li>Loss of concentration, manifested as forgetfulness, clumsiness, difficulty in</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>making decisions and insomnia (poor sleep).</p>
<ul>
<li>Miscellaneous symptoms, including feelings of suffocation, chest pains, heart pounding, numbness and tingling sensation.</li>
</ul>
<p>Patients with the symptoms of PMT can be relieved by giving them diuretics, for example, chlorothiazide in the pre menstrual week. They can also benefit from oral contraceptives, for instance, progesterones like norethisterone 20mg daily from the 15th to 25th day of the cycle.</p>
<p>Tranquillisers and psychotherapy also appear to be equally effective.</p>
<p>Patients should be told about the physiology that is producing these symptoms because they may think they have a terrible disease and the worries may increase the intensity of these symptoms.</p>
<p>Dietary management involves taking a low salt diet and avoiding alcohol and caffeine.</p>
<p>Exercise is also recommended to relieve the symptoms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dysfunctional-uterine-bleeding-dub">Dysfunctional Uterine Bleeding (DUB)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dysfunctional-uterine-bleeding-dub" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Dysfunctional uterine bleeding is diagnosed by exclusion of the conditions, which cause bleeding from the uterus. The conditions to be excluded include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Infection</li>
<li>Ruptured ectopic pregnancy</li>
<li>Trauma</li>
<li>Uterine fibroids and polyps</li>
<li>Genital cancers</li>
<li>Hormonal treatment</li>
</ul>
<p>Once you have excluded the conditions mentioned above, the cause of DUB is most likely to be hormonal imbalance, which is associated with involuntary periods. As there is very little you can do, you should refer all patients with abnormal uterine bleeding to the hospital for investigations and management.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If the patient is very sick due to excessive bleeding, then resuscitate and give intravenous fluids before referring.</p>
<p>In the hospital, teenage girls who have just started menstruating should be given a combination of oestrogen and progesterone. The contraceptive pill is a good option and treatment should be continued for three to six</p>
<p>cycles. After treatment is stopped, menstruation often returns to normal.</p>
<p>For women in the reproductive age group, true dysfunctional bleeding is uncommon. The most likely cause of abnormal bleeding at this age is some complication of pregnancy. Diagnostic curettage is needed and you must remember the possibility of malignant disease.</p>
<p>In women over 40 years of age all the organic causes of bleeding, including malignant disease, may occur. Accurate diagnosis, including curettage is essential.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="menorrhagia">Menorrhagia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#menorrhagia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Menorrhagia is a normal cycle with an excessive loss of blood (heavy menstrual flow). The normal average volume of menstrual loss is approximately 70ml. Menstrual loss is naturally greater in parous women.</p>
<p>Menorrhagia is clinically an important condition because this excessive bleeding results in anaemia. It is not a disease but a symptom and to treat it one must find out what is causing it. The best way to manage this condition is to refer the patient to hospital where investigations will be carried out and managed appropriately.</p>
<p>The most common causes of menorrhagia include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fibroids due to a larger endometrial cavity hence larger bleeding areas</li>
<li>Chronic PID</li>
<li>Endometrial polyps</li>
<li>Abnormalities in the blood clotting power, for example, leukaemia, thrombocytopenic purpura</li>
<li>Abnormal hormonal state, leading to excessively thick endometrium, which bleeds heavily when shed</li>
<li>Emotional factors, which can sometimes cause heavy bleeding</li>
<li>Intrauterine contraceptive devices</li>
</ul>
<p>Some of these conditions will be discussed in a later part of this unit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-menorrhagia">Management of Menorrhagia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-menorrhagia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The management of this condition includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>History taking followed by pelvic examination.</li>
<li>Investigations of blood for abnormalities and checking Hb, grouping and cross-matching.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Dilatation and curettage under general anaesthetic. This procedure may be curative if there is not any other abnormality. The patient should be prepared preoperatively and postoperative care should be provided as for any other surgical procedure.</li>
<li>Older women can be better treated by a hysterectomy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="metrorrhagia">Metrorrhagia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#metrorrhagia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is menstrual bleeding lasting too long. It is caused by irregular shedding of the endometrium because the corpus luteum degenerates too slowly and the progesterone effect persists. Some secretory endometrium is still present early in the following cycle.</p>
<p>The causes of this disorder are:</p>
<ul>
<li>The possibility of cancer of the genital tract with this kind of bleeding.</li>
<li>Uterine polyps projecting into the vagina may cause bleeding.</li>
<li>Incomplete evacuation after abortion.</li>
<li>Hydatid form mole.</li>
<li>Chorion carcinoma.</li>
<li>Occasionally women on oral contraceptives may have what is called 'break through bleeding'.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-metrorrhagia">Management of Metrorrhagia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-metrorrhagia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The management will include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Taking a detailed history.</li>
<li>Performing a digital examination and speculum to visualise the cervix and even take a Pap smear, therefore, the patient should be referred to the gynaecologist as soon as possible.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong>
Never dismiss metrorrhagia lightly. A thorough examination should be performed.</p>
