<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="epimenorrhoea">Epimenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epimenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is when normal menstruation occurs too often due to a shortened luteal phase by early degeneration of the corpus luteum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-epimenorrhoea">Management of Epimenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-epimenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The management of this condition will include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A detailed history to establish the cause.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Refer all patients with abnormal bleeding to hospital for investigations and treatment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In the hospital teenage girls who have just started menstruating should be treated with a combination of oestrogen and progesterone contraceptive pill, which should be continued for three to six cycles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Meanwhile the patient should also be given iron to help replace any blood lost.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In women of the reproductive age group, diagnostic curettage is needed. Remember the possibility of malignant diseases.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Curettage may cure the condition, but if it does not, a hysterectomy may be the best option leaving the ovaries intact.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hypomenorrhoea">Hypomenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypomenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is when the period occurs on a regular basis but is minimal. For example, there are rare cases whereby a woman menstruates regularly twice or thrice in a year. This is considered to be normal although you may be able to guess what problems this woman may have? This will be covered later in this unit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="endometriosis-or-adenomyosis">Endometriosis or Adenomyosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endometriosis-or-adenomyosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This condition is as a result of the endometrial tissue being deposited in any organ of the body, for example, the ovary or uterosacral ligaments.</p>
<p>The ectopic tissue consists of both glands and stroma in which cyclical menstrual changes occur. Malignant changes are very rare. The process where the endometrial tissues invade the myometrium in the uterus is referred to as internal endometriosis or adenomyosis (the uterus is enlarged). There is no difference clinically between adenomyosis and fibroids on feeling the uterus, but they are different histologically.</p>
<p>Endometriosis occurs only in tissues adjacent to the Mullerian systems (a pair of ducts in the female foetus which develop into reproductive system). The theories, which explain the occurrence of endometriosis include that it may be disseminated by means of the lymphatic and vascular system, which is why endometrial tissue may be found in the umbilicus, forearm and thigh.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="endometriosis-or-adenomyosis">Endometriosis or Adenomyosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endometriosis-or-adenomyosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Endometriosis is also strangely common in social groups where childbearing is delayed to the late twenties or early thirties. This might explain why it is rarely diagnosed before the age of 20 years and not apparent after menopause.</p>
<p>Physical signs will depend on the site of the disease and they include:</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 245 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>'Chocolate cysts' which are tender, fixed, bilateral masses, resembling chronic salpingo-ophritis but without any history of infection, fever or discharge.</p>
<ul>
<li>Uterine lesions may cause nodular or uniform uterine enlargement and may be clinically indistinguishable from fibromyomata or diffuse hyperplasia.</li>
<li>Recto-vaginal lesions are tender, hard fixed and simulate rectal carcinoma.</li>
<li>Local lesion, for example, in scars may be tender at menstrual periods.</li>
<li>Dysmenorrhoea occurs and any palpable tumour may become painful at the time of the menstruation.</li>
<li>Recto-vaginal lesions will cause dyspareunia.</li>
<li>Menorrhagia and irregular bleeding occur from associated endometrial hyperplasia or from uterine lesions.</li>
<li>Infertility occurs in 30% of patients with endometriosis and this is due to pelvic adhesions or endometrial abnormalities.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-endometriosis">Management of Endometriosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-endometriosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The first step is to take a detailed history to elicit the symptoms of dysmenorrhoea, menorrhagia and dyspareunia. There are rarely abnormal findings on abdominal examination.</p>
<p>Refer the patient to a gynaecologist. On vaginal examination, the uterus may be enlarged and tender (adenomyosis). Areas around the ovaries are tender and, characteristically, there is limited mobility of uterus. A cyst is sometimes palpable in either fornix.</p>
<p>Speculum examination may reveal typical areas of endometriosis in the cervix or vaginal vault. A laparotomy is indicated when cystic swelling is felt or if you are in doubt of the diagnosis.</p>
<p>If the patient is under 40 years of age, surgical treatment is usually designed to destroy areas of endometriosis using diathermy function. Hormonal therapy should include either progesterone steroids when confirmed, administered either cyclically or continuously for three to twelve months (this therapy suppresses the residual areas). Pregnancy is another way of suppressing the condition, and often has a curative effect on endometriosis.</p>
<p>Patients over 40 years of age may undergo a hysterectomy, which can include the removal of the affected ovary since hormonal therapy is not always helpful.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-3-bleeding-disorders-in-pregnancy">SECTION 3: BLEEDING DISORDERS IN PREGNANCY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-3-bleeding-disorders-in-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In this section you will look at bleeding disorders in pregnancy. These conditions are usually on the borderline between obstetrics and gynaecology, in the sense that they involve women whose pregnancy comes to a premature end. You will find that these patients are always treated in a gynaecological ward rather than in the maternity ward.</p>
<p>For the purposes of this unit, bleeding in pregnancy refers to any bleeding per vagina. This bleeding, however slight, should be taken seriously. It is sometimes the first sign of some of the most life-threatening emergencies in obstetrics such as ruptured ectopic, and incomplete abortion. You will look at the possible causes of bleeding per vagina during pregnancy, how each case presents, and how it should be managed. The procedure known as Manual Vacuum Aspiration (MVA) as part of post-abortal care will also be covered.</p>
<p>It is important for you to note that bleeding per vagina during pregnancy is a cause for concern to most mothers. This is particularly so in a mother who has had a previous experience of vaginal bleeding which resulted in foetal loss. You must, therefore, be aware of the mother's emotional situation when caring for her during the antepartum period.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>State the different types of abortion</li>
<li>Specify the causes of abortions</li>
<li>Describe the management of at least three types of abortion</li>
<li>Describe signs and symptoms of ruptured ectopic</li>
<li>Describe the management of ruptured ectopic</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="bleeding-in-early-pregnancy">Bleeding in Early Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bleeding-in-early-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Vaginal bleeding in early pregnancy refers to any bleeding per vagina that occurs before the 28th week of pregnancy. In the early months of pregnancy, bleeding may be due to a number of factors or conditions.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 246 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 247 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="name-three-conditions-that-cause-bleeding-in-early-pregnancy">Name three conditions that cause bleeding in early pregnancy.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#name-three-conditions-that-cause-bleeding-in-early-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Did you think of any of the following conditions?</p>
<ul>
<li>Abortion</li>
<li>Ectopic pregnancy</li>
<li>Hydatidiform mole</li>
<li>Chorion carcinoma</li>
</ul>
<p>As you may know, the most common cause of bleeding in early pregnancy is abortion. Abortion accounts for 95% of all bleeding in early pregnancy, whilst all the others account for only 5%. The last two, that is hydatidiform mole and chorion carcinoma will be discussed in the last section of this unit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="abortion">Abortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Abortion is defined as the loss or expulsion of the foetus before the 20th week of pregnancy. Abortion is significant not only because of the loss of a wanted pregnancy, but because it is a major cause of maternal death from the haemorrhage and sepsis that may follow a mismanaged abortion.</p>
<p>The definition of abortion generally accepted for legal purposes is 'the delivery of a foetus at less than 20 weeks gestation or with foetal weight of less than 500gm'.</p>
<p>Many people tend to look upon abortion as pregnancy that has been terminated criminally and miscarriage as a spontaneous occurrence. As a result, abortion is stigmatised, however, the two are the same thing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-abortion">Causes of Abortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The causes of abortion are many and are divided into maternal, foetal and miscellaneous causes.</p>
<p>Maternal causes of abortion account for about 25% of the known cases of abortions and they include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>General diseases like hypertension or chronic heart disease.</li>
<li>Acute febrile illnesses, for example, malaria, acute pyelonephritis, pneumonia.</li>
<li>Endocrine disorders, for example, thyrotoxicosis, poorly controlled diabetes mellitus.</li>
<li>Local conditions such as under development of the uterus, fibroids and congenital abnormalities of the uterus. The fibroids can cause abortions, especially if they are submucous or deeply intramural. The congenital abnormalities of the uterus include a septate uterus and a bicornuate (uterus divided into two) uterus.</li>
<li>Cervical incompetence which may be due to either congenital weakness of the circular muscle fibres of the cervix, or previous splitting of the cervical sphincter due to obstetrical trauma, or high amputation of the cervix due to cervical lesions.</li>
</ul>
<p>Foetal causes of abortion account for about 75% of the known cases and they often result in early abortion, that is, first trimester abortions. Foetal causes may be due to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Chromosomal or genetic abnormalities.</li>
<li>Abnormal attachment of the placenta, that is, defective implantation or activity of the trophoblast.</li>
</ul>
<p>In addition to maternal and foetal causes, there are those that are grouped as</p>
<p>miscellaneous causes. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Accidents, for example, falls, and injuries. The incidence of abortion among these cases varies enormously from individual to individual after the accidents.</li>
<li>Criminal interference, using various instruments, local herbs and plastic catheters, which are inserted into the cervical canal.</li>
<li>An Intrauterine Contraceptive Device (IUCD). An abortion, especially in the second trimester can occur if conception occurs despite the presence of an IUCD. Note that ectopic pregnancy, antepartum haemorrhage, premature rupture of the membranes and manual removal of the placenta occurs more commonly in pregnancy with an IUCD. Therefore, the IUCD should be removed as soon as pregnancy is diagnosed.</li>
</ul>
<p>Most of these abortions occur in the first three months of the pregnancy, before the placenta is mature. Abortion is the detachment of the products of conception, which is accompanied by bleeding that may be profuse. Blood loss is accompanied by painful contractions of the uterus, dilation of the cervix and expulsion of the foetus and its membranes. Slight or even moderate bleeding does not, however, mean that the foetus is no longer alive. As a health worker you must do all you can to save life at all times.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 248 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="types-of-abortion">Types of Abortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>As you can see there are many different types of abortion.</p>
<ul>
<li>Threatened Abortion</li>
<li>Inevitable or Imminent Abortion</li>
<li>Missed Abortion</li>
<li>Habitual Abortion</li>
<li>Septic Abortion</li>
<li>Induced Abortion</li>
</ul>
<p>Now move on to look at the different types of abortions and how they are managed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="threatened-abortion">Threatened Abortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#threatened-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The patient with threatened abortion will have slight vaginal bleeding and abdominal discomfort. When you examine her you will find the os of the cervix closed.</p>
<p>While many patients will successfully carry this type of pregnancy to term, others may not. It is essential, therefore, to make the patient realise that nothing can be done to prevent an abortion.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-291ff668.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<p>Threatened
Slight placental separation,
slight bleeding, os closed.</p>
<p>Here are some essential measures to take:</p>
<ul>
<li>Reassure the patient that, if she continues with the pregnancy, the foetus will not be at greater risk of abnormalities and that it will continue to grow just like in a normal pregnancy.</li>
<li>Ensure bed rest and allay anxiety (of losing the pregnancy) by administering tabs. Phenobarbitone 30 to 60 mgs tds, morphine 10 mgs or pethidine 100 mgs.</li>
</ul>
<p>If the pain is stronger, some doctors may use progesterone.</p>
<ul>
<li>Warn the patient to notify the medical team if the cramps become worse or the bleeding becomes heavy.</li>
<li>Ask her to save the pads as well as any tissue or clots that she might expel, for examination.</li>
<li>Advise her to take a low residue diet and avoid aperients and enema because this will stimulate the contractions.</li>
<li>Advise her to remain in bed for at least three days after the bleeding stops.</li>
<li>Advise her to avoid heavy physical activities and especially sexual excitement.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Vaginal examination is NOT usually carried out because of fear of increasing uterine disturbance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="inevitable-or-imminent-abortion">Inevitable or Imminent Abortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inevitable-or-imminent-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Inevitable or imminent abortion means that nothing else can be done. The foetus must come out. The abortion becomes inevitable if, in addition to vaginal bleeding and abdominal discomfort, the uterine contractions become strong and painful and lead to dilatation of the cervix. This is followed by either complete abortion or incomplete abortion.</p>
<p>The primary measure taken is to save the life of the patient since there is often profuse bleeding, especially in patients who end up with an incomplete abortion. Take the patient's history to determine if the products of conception have been expelled.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-d87005f9.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<p>Incomplete Abortion Placenta and membranes are retained. Foetus is expelled.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="inevitable-or-imminent-abortion">Inevitable or Imminent Abortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inevitable-or-imminent-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Many patients will come to the hospital due to severe bleeding, which means that the products of conception have been retained. Since there is essentially no chance of the pregnancy progressing any further under these circumstances, the uterus should be emptied immediately.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Resuscitate all patients with shock first, before transferring them to a hospital.</p>
<p>If the patient has excessive blood loss, hasten the evacuation by administering an oxytocic drug. Bleeding that does not cease after the expulsion of the products of conception will require administration of ergometrine 0.5mg stat. Take blood for grouping and cross-matching then fix a drip of plasma expanders or normal saline/Hartman's solution. Give a strong analgesic to relieve pain. Severe pain can lead to shock.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-80fe7963.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg">
Complete abortion Placenta, foetus and membranes are all expelled.</p>
<p>Save anything passed per vagina to inspect if all products of conception have been passed. Observe infection prevention principles while performing vaginal examinations to remove any placenta tissues distending the cervix.</p>
<p>A finger or sponge forceps is used to remove the products of conception. Observe bleeding and if the temperature is normal after the evacuation of contents, the patient can be discharged.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="missed-abortion">Missed Abortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#missed-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This means that the products of conception are not expelled despite the signs and symptoms of abortion. It occurs when abortion is threatened but the bleeding ceases and all is apparently well, except that signs of pregnancy subside, breast activity stops, and the uterus does not grow bigger.</p>
<p>After some time (about eight weeks) a brownish discharge from the vagina appears. This shows that the foetus is dead but still in the uterus. It degenerates into a solid mass of mostly organised blood clot called a carneous mole. This mole will in time be expelled with little or no loss of blood. This may be hastened by the administration of ergot and stilbesterol by mouth. Refer all suspected cases of missed abortion to hospital for management as it may be necessary to carry out a surgical evacuation as well as to check the uterus for any abnormalities by performing an ultrasound.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-a2fd776f.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg">
Missed Abortion Foetus is dead and there is retained placenta. There is also a brown vaginal discharge.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="habitual-abortion">Habitual Abortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#habitual-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is when a woman has had three or more successive abortions. In the majority of cases, the cause is not obvious. Some of the known causes however, include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Chronic illness, for example, diabetes mellitus.</li>
<li>Abnormalities, for example, septate uterus and cervical incompetence being the most common, especially in late abortions.</li>
<li>Endocrine or genetic causes, especially if it occurs before 14 weeks.</li>
<li>Infections, for example, syphilis.</li>
</ul>
<p>In the management of this patient, the following is performed:</p>
<ul>
<li>Take history and carry out a physical examination to establish the cause.</li>
<li>Deal with the causes that can be managed, for example, if it is syphilis then treat.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 249 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Advise on proper dietary intake, together with thyroid and hormonal supplements (but not diethylstilbestrol or other oestrogens).</li>
<li>Establish a therapeutic supportive relationship with the patient to help her overcome the loss of her pregnancy.</li>
<li>Surgically correct the obvious abnormalities of the genital tract, like removal of myomas and repair of an incompetent cervix.</li>
<li>Provide appropriate pre and postoperative care as for any other surgical patient.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="septic-abortion">Septic Abortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#septic-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the past, this type of abortion was associated with the criminal interference of a pregnancy. However, it may occur in a spontaneous abortion, if there has been bacterial contamination. Septic abortion is usually caused by gram-negative Escherichia Coli (E. Coli) but sometimes gram-positive streptococci and staphylococci are also involved. In most cases, the infection is mild and limited to the uterus.</p>
<p>The infection may be limited to the tubes or it may spread to the peritoneal cavity and cause peritonitis. Severe E. Coli infection may lead to septicaemic shock due to endotoxins released by the organism, thus leading to total vascular collapse (death).</p>
<p>The patient will present with:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fever due to the infection</li>
<li>Fast, rapid pulse rate due to the infection and fever</li>
<li>Offensive smelling vaginal discharge</li>
<li>Tender lower abdomen on palpation</li>
<li>Bright red blood continues to be lost</li>
</ul>
<p>The management will include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Resuscitating with intravenous fluids.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administering antibiotics, both broad spectrum and perinatally.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Evacuating infected products of conception as soon as possible.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Taking history with an emphasis on why the abortion was performed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Taking relevant specimens for investigation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ruling out infection in other systems.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Assessing urinary output to rule out renal function interference.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monitoring vital signs carefully since a high temperature and rapid pulse will indicate the severity of the infection.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Taking cervical swab for culture and sensitivity in order to institute treatment according to the findings.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Encouraging plenty of fluid intake in order to flush the system of the toxins and correct dehydration.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Performing vulva toilet four hourly with antiseptic.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administering tetanus toxoid or anti-tetanus serum 0.5 mls for treatment.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="induced-abortion">Induced Abortion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#induced-abortion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Induced abortion is an abortion that is intentionally caused. It is commonly associated with young unmarried women, especially schoolgirls or even married women who get pregnant due to contraceptive failure. However, an induced abortion can also be performed for medical reasons.</p>
<p>There are two types of induced abortion: Therapeutic (which is performed on medical grounds) and Criminal (which is illegal).</p>
<p>According to medical ethics, a <strong>therapeutic abortion</strong> may be carried out only if two registered medical practitioners are of the opinion that the pregnancy should be terminated. There are two specific circumstances when this can be done. These are:</p>
<ul>
<li>If the continuance of the pregnancy would involve a risk to the life of the pregnant woman or of injury to her physical or mental health.</li>
<li>If there is a substantial risk that the child, when born, would suffer from physical or mental abnormalities and be seriously handicapped.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Criminal abortions</strong> are sometimes attempted by an unqualified person. The operation is often hurried and lacking asepsis. The complications of criminal abortions include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Haemorrhage.</li>
<li>Sepsis, which is usually severe and can lead to septicaemia and endotoxin shock.</li>
<li>Haemolysis and renal damage may occur secondary to the septicaemia.</li>
<li>Injuries to the birth canal and pelvic organs.</li>
<li>Sudden death due to extreme syncope as a result of dilatation of the</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>cervix and in some cases from amniotic embolism.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong>
According to the laws of this country, induced abortion is a criminal offence, unless it is done on medical grounds.</p>
<p>The illustration below shows the outcome of therapeutic and threatened abortions. Note that threatened abortions are usually spontaneous.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-313c6111.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg"></p>
<p><strong>Post-Abortal Care (PAC)</strong></p>
<p>PAC comprises the comprehensive health care provided to patients with problems of incomplete abortion. It has three interrelated components, which are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Emergency treatment of complications arising from spontaneous or induced abortion.</li>
<li>Family planning counselling and services.</li>
<li>Access to comprehensive reproductive health care.</li>
</ul>
<p>These are the major components for PAC, which various health care providers/groups may provide.</p>
<p>You should ensure the control and prevention of cross-infection when performing procedures. Thus, it is important to remember the infection prevention principles, which you covered in the previous unit on Contraceptive Technology.</p>
<p><strong>Care After Manual Vacuum Aspiration (MVA)</strong></p>
<p>You should check the patient's vital signs, severe vaginal bleeding and general condition and allow the patient to rest comfortably.</p>
<p>Patients that have been treated should receive after care guidance, which includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain/counsel patient before discharge that she will be at risk of repeat pregnancy for up to two weeks following treatment.</li>
<li>Counsel her on a variety of safe contraceptive methods that can be used immediately to avoid pregnancy for the body to return to its normal state.</li>
<li>Explain where and how to get family planning.</li>
<li>Counsel on all available family planning methods to enable the patient to make an informed choice of family planning methods.</li>
<li>Explain how to use the selected family planning method.</li>
<li>Explain that family planning methods, other than condoms do not provide protection against STI/HIV/AIDS.</li>
</ul>
<p>As mentioned on the previous page, patients that have been treated should receive after care guidance, which also includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Informing her about symptoms that would require the patient to return immediately to the facility and the action she should take.</li>
<li>Advising her on signs of recovery when normal menstruation may resume.</li>
<li>Advising her on personal hygiene and when to resume sex.</li>
<li>Providing the method of choice to the patient.</li>
<li>Helping the patient to cope with the pregnancy loss.</li>
<li>Allowing grieving.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Ectopic Pregnancy (Extrauterine Pregnancy)</strong></p>
<p>Ectopic pregnancy is a condition in which the zygote becomes implanted in a place outside the uterine cavity. The most common site of ectopic gestation is inside one of the fallopian tubes and this is called a tubal pregnancy. The term ectopic is derived from a Greek word, which means 'out of place'.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Can you remember the other sites where the zygote can implant outside the uterine cavity?</p>
<p>Did you remember the other less common sites?</p>
<p>The ovary
The cervix
The abdominal cavity</p>
<p>The illustration below shows the different possible locations of an ectopic pregnancy with relative frequency occurrence.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Key</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>A</td><td>Ampulla</td></tr><tr><td>Cx</td><td>Cervix</td></tr><tr><td>F</td><td>Fimbrial</td></tr><tr><td>I</td><td>Interstitial</td></tr><tr><td>Ov</td><td>Ovary</td></tr><tr><td>C</td><td>Cornua</td></tr><tr><td>Is</td><td>Isthmus</td></tr><tr><td>Ab</td><td>Abdominal Cavity</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-dc519d58.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg"></p>
<p>The most common type of ectopic pregnancy is the tubal pregnancy, occurring in at least 55% of ectopic pregnancies. This type of pregnancy is common in the tropics because of the high incidence of blocked tubes due to gonorrhoea, puerperal and post abortal sepsis, and Pelvic Inflammatory Diseases (PIDs).</p>
<p>The ovum is fertilised in the fallopian tube but the zygote is unable to reach the uterine cavity because of loss of mobility and ciliary action. Therefore, the ovum may be arrested at:</p>
<ul>
<li>The fimbriated end of the tube, which is an uncommon site.</li>
<li>The ampulla which is the most common site.</li>
<li>The isthmus which is the most dangerous site because of the</li>
</ul>
<p>frequency of tubal rupture at about four to five weeks.</p>
<ul>
<li>The interstitial part of the tube in which rupture begins at second trimester. It is also an uncommon site.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-6edba1d6.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"></p>
<p>In many African countries, including Kenya, ruptured tubal pregnancy is the most common surgical emergency in women. Consequently, it is very important that you know how this condition presents and how it is managed.</p>
<p>From the description of the types of ectopic pregnancies you can now easily identify their causes.</p>
<p>Some of the common causes of ectopic pregnancy include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Previous inflammatory process in the tube or acute PID, which will heal with scarring tissue and block the tube.</li>
<li>Peritoneal adhesions secondary to previous surgery due to, for example, appendicitis, may cause occlusion.</li>
<li>Endometriosis whereby the endometrial tissue is lodged in the tube and occludes the tubal lumen.</li>
<li>Congenital anatomical irregularity often due to presence of diverticula of the uterine tube.</li>
<li>Tubal surgery.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology-of-ectopic-pregnancy">Pathophysiology of Ectopic Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology-of-ectopic-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Once the implantation has occurred in the tube, the sequence of events associated with pregnancy follows. The corpus luteum remains and grows, producing progesterone, which</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>increases the thickness of the endometrium and ensures that it is not shed, so that the patient misses the period.</p>
<p>The tube is not, however, able to nourish the ovum for long and bleeding detaches the ovum. The ovum may be ejected into the peritoneal cavity through the fimbriated end. The onset of pain may be gradual or it may occur dramatically.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="symptoms-and-signs-of-ectopic-pregnancy">Symptoms and Signs of Ectopic Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-and-signs-of-ectopic-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Unfortunately, an ectopic pregnancy causes very few symptoms until the foetus has become large enough to rupture the fallopian tube. This, therefore, makes it very difficult to diagnose an ectopic pregnancy before it ruptures. That is why it is very important that you refer a patient to hospital on the slightest suspicion of ectopic pregnancy.</p>
<p>The muscle wall of the tube does not have the capacity of the uterine muscle for hypertrophy and distension and tubal pregnancies nearly always end in rupture and the death of the ovum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="before-rupture">Before Rupture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#before-rupture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should suspect an ectopic pregnancy before rupture if a woman comes to you with the following complaints:</p>
<ul>
<li>Amenorrhoea of two or three months (common in about 80% of cases). The patient may sometimes present with a ruptured ectopic even before the expected date of the next period.</li>
<li>Vague lower abdominal pain, which the patient might ignore. This is due to slight leakage of blood from the tube, which causes localised peritoneal irritation. It may also be due to the distension of the tube by the growing foetus.</li>
</ul>
<p>On examination the patient is usually healthy. You might feel a slightly enlarged uterus or a mass on one side of the uterus.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-24a8368c.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg">
Rupture into Lumen of Tube
Tubal Abortion</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="after-rupture">After Rupture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#after-rupture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When the tubal pregnancy ruptures, usually after two to three months, the patient presents with the following complaints. For the acute type of rupture, also known as fulminating, they complain of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sudden onset of low abdominal pain.</li>
<li>Vomiting and fainting because of the sudden intraperitoneal bleeding.</li>
<li>Vaginal bleeding, this may not develop until many hours after the rupture.</li>
<li>If bleeding is rapid it may lead to hypotension and shock.</li>
</ul>
<p>For the chronic leaking type, the patient complains of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Suffering for some time from abdominal uneasiness.</li>
<li>Pain.</li>
<li>Occasional fainting.</li>
<li>Haemorrhagic slight bleeding.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-983fbaef.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg">
Rupture into the Peritoneal Cavity</p>
<p>The chronic rupture is the most common type of rupture of tubal pregnancy that you are likely to encounter. Unfortunately, in many cases, whenever health workers talk about an ectopic pregnancy, they only think of the acute type, that</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>is a woman who develops sudden severe abdominal pain and collapses.</p>
<p>You must remember that not all ectopic pregnancies present in the acute type. In fact, in clinical practice, some of these patients have been wrongly managed as either threatened abortion or acute pelvic inflammatory disease. That is why an ectopic pregnancy has been called 'the great deceiver'.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong>
Diagnostic errors of an ectopic pregnancy may be fatal.</p>
<p>Now move on to look at each of the two clinical types of ruptured ectopic pregnancy</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="acute-rupture-of-ectopic-pregnancy">Acute Rupture of Ectopic Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-rupture-of-ectopic-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A woman with acute ectopic pregnancy may present as discussed earlier with the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sudden onset of lower abdominal pain.</li>
<li>Vomiting and fainting because of the sudden intraperitoneal bleeding.</li>
<li>Vaginal bleeding, though this may not develop until some hours after rupture of the tube and the death of the foetus.</li>
</ul>
<p>On examination you might detect the following signs:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The patient is in agonising pain and is restless.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>She is sweating, yet her skin feels cold and her palms are wet.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>She yawns frequently as if hungry for air.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The radial pulse is rapid, weak and thready. The blood pressure may be very low or unrecordable.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The temperature is usually normal.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The abdomen is very tender with muscle guarding. Signs of free fluid in the peritoneal cavity, such as a fluid thrill and shifting dullness, might be detected if the patient can tolerate the examination. However, the absence of these signs does not mean that there is no free blood in the peritoneal cavity as the blood might be in small amounts.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A pelvic examination is very painful and it is difficult to palpate the organs properly so it is important that you remember to be very gentle.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There is extreme pain on moving the cervix with the examining fingers, that is, the cervix is excitable.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The uterus is often slightly enlarged and a tender mass might be felt on one side of the uterus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A tender mass may also be palpated in the pouch of Douglas if blood is clotted there. This is also known as pelvic haematocele.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient is usually anaemic.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong>
A sudden, severe collapse with little or no warning signs generally occurs when the zygote is implanted in the isthmus and there may be no history of a missed menstrual period.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="differential-diagnosis-of-the-acute-ruptured-ectopic-pregnancy">Differential Diagnosis of the Acute Ruptured Ectopic Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#differential-diagnosis-of-the-acute-ruptured-ectopic-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A ruptured ectopic gestation may be confused with many other conditions such as acute pelvic inflammatory disease, rupture of a gastric or duodenal ulcer, fulminating appendicitis, torsion of the pedicle of an ovarian cyst, acute pyelonephritis and/or rupture of a corpus luteum with intraperitoneal haemorrhage.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong>
In abortion, bleeding usually precedes pain, while in ruptured tubal pregnancy pain almost invariably precedes bleeding.</p>

Uterus slightly enlarged, irregularly softened, tender with infection</td></tr><tr><td>Laboratory Findings</td><td>WBC count raised; RBC count strikingly low if blood loss is large; Sedimentation rate slightly elevated</td><td>WBC count rarely normal; RBC count normal; Sedimentation rate slightly elevated</td><td>WBC count raised; RBC count normal; Sedimentation rate markedly elevated</td><td>WBC count normal, if spontaneous and raised if induced (infection); Sedimentation rate slight to moderately elevated</td></tr><tr><td>Menstruation</td><td>Some aberration; Missed period; spotting</td><td>Unrelated to menses</td><td>Hypermenorrhoea or metrorrhagia or both</td><td>Amenorrhoea then spotting then brisk bleeding</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In the next sub-section you will study the symptoms and signs of chronic leaking ectopic pregnancy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chronic-leaking-ectopic-pregnancy">Chronic Leaking Ectopic Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chronic-leaking-ectopic-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this type of pregnancy, it is very important to note the clinical history of the patient. You should check for the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Abdominal pain and uneasiness, where the pain is generally situated low down in the abdomen and, often, is more marked on one side. It is continuous and is not relieved by pressure, as is the case in intestinal colic. Sometimes the act of emptying the bladder initiates a bout of pain. In a few cases the patient</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>complains of a frequent inclination to go and pass stool.</p>
<ul>
<li>Amenorrhoea is usually present, with irregular vaginal bleeding, which is usually slight and often dark brown in colour. It is not uncommon to attribute this discharge to threatened abortion.</li>
<li>Occasionally there is expulsion of a decidual cast, especially if the pregnancy has gone beyond two months. The patient will give you an impression that she had a miscarriage. In some cases the health worker may carry out an evacuation thinking the patient has experienced an incomplete abortion.</li>
<li>Occasionally there is a feeling of nausea, vomiting and fainting attacks. Remember that sudden faintness is a characteristic symptom of ectopic gestation.</li>
</ul>
<p>When you examine the patient you are likely to find the following signs:</p>
<ul>
<li>Anaemia of variable degrees.</li>
<li>Rapid pulse.</li>
<li>Normal or low blood pressure.</li>
<li>General tenderness and guarding in the lower abdomen, which is more marked on one side.</li>
<li>There may be a tender, firm mass in one of the iliac fossae.</li>
<li>On vaginal examination you will feel a tender mass in one of the fornices.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-ectopic-pregnancy">Management of Ectopic Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-ectopic-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A patient with tubal pregnancy will require an emergency operation. The patient should be immediately referred to a hospital. Start an intravenous drip of normal saline before transferring the patient. During the transfer, ensure that you treat the patient for shock and administer analgesics like morphine or pethidine for the pain. Potential blood donors should accompany the patient to hospital where possible.</p>
<p>In the hospital, the following diagnostic tests may be performed:</p>
<ul>
<li>Ultrasonography.</li>
<li>Culdocentesis whereby non-clotting blood will be aspirated from the cul-de-sac.</li>
<li>Human Chorionic Gonadorophin (HCG), which involves urine testing.</li>
</ul>
<p>Blood is taken for grouping and cross-matching and a blood transfusion is started. An emergency laparatomy is then performed to ligate the bleeders. The affected tube is usually removed by salpingectomy or salpingotomy, which involves making an opening in the tube.</p>
<p>It may be possible to give an auto-transfusion to a patient with a fresh rupture of a tubal pregnancy. Auto-transfusion involves scooping blood from the opened abdomen with a small gallipot and pouring it through a filter made of three or four layers of gauze into a sterile bowel or jug containing sodium acid citrate solution, which is an anti-coagulant. When 500ml of blood have been collected it is decanted into a sterile bottle, which is then set up on a drip that is already running. Sometimes the blood is aspirated directly from the peritoneal cavity into a plastic transfusion bag containing sodium citrate solution.</p>
<p>Auto-transfusion is not advisable if:</p>
<ul>
<li>The history of the patient suggests that heavy bleeding began more than 24 hours before the operation.</li>
<li>The blood appears discoloured or haemolysed.</li>
<li>There is an offensive odour when the abdomen is opened.</li>
</ul>
<p>The advantages of auto-transfusion include:</p>
<ul>
<li>No risk of transmitting HIV.</li>
<li>Blood is easily available and perfectly compatible.</li>
</ul>
<p>However serious the patient's condition appears to be, this operation has an excellent success rate. Post-operatively, the patient should be managed in the same manner as for any other abdominal operation.</p>
<p>After surgical treatment, there are several potential outcomes.</p>
<ul>
<li>Another tubal pregnancy will occur in about 10% of the cases treated.</li>
<li>Infertility develops in approximately half of the patients who have undergone surgery for the treatment of an ectopic pregnancy. Of these about 30% become sterile.</li>
<li>Normal pregnancies are achieved in about half of patients who have one ectopic pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 256 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 257 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section-4-genital-disorders-and-injuries">SECTION 4: GENITAL DISORDERS AND INJURIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-4-genital-disorders-and-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this section, you are going to look at some disorders of the genital tract and injuries. They shall be explained under the following grouping:</p>
<ul>
<li>Vulva dystrophies and cysts</li>
<li>Relaxation of pelvic support</li>
<li>Traumatic disorders of the genital organs</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this section, you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain dystrophies and cysts affecting the genital tract</li>
<li>State the causes and management of relaxation of pelvic muscles</li>
<li>Describe the management and prevention of trauma to genital organs</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vulva-dystrophies-and-cysts">Vulva Dystrophies and Cysts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vulva-dystrophies-and-cysts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Dystrophy refers to the defective nutrition of an organ or tissue, usually muscle. There are various types of dystrophies and these will now be explained in detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="atrophic-lesions">Atrophic Lesions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#atrophic-lesions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is due to ageing when there is a decrease in endogenous oestrogen. Atrophic changes in the vulva skin and sub-dermal tissues usually occur after some years.</p>
<p>Lichen sclerosis is a systemic dermatological condition and the most common cause of atrophic dystrophy. There will be contractures of the vaginal introitus and the skin becomes thin, fragile and easily traumatised. Its chief symptoms include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Dysuria</li>
<li>Pruritis</li>
<li>Dyspareunia</li>
</ul>
<p>The vulva is the skin surface most frequently affected, although the skin of the back, axilla and beneath the arms may also be affected.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hypertrophic-dystrophies">Hypertrophic Dystrophies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypertrophic-dystrophies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Chronic irritation or vulvo-vaginal infection may result in benign epithelial thickening and hyperkeratosis. During the acute phases, as in diabetic vulvitis, the lesions may be red and moist, which provide evidence of secondary infection. The lesions may involve any portion of the vulva, adjacent thighs, perineum or perineal skin.</p>
<p>Invasive malignancies may also appear as white lesions of the vulvar skin. A biopsy should be able to detect whether malignancy exists or not. Periodic re-examination of specimen biopsies and the excision of more advanced lesions should be performed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-lesions">Management of Lesions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-lesions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The atrophic lesions and hypertrophic dystrophy lesions are both treated in the same manner.</p>
<p>Pruritis, dyspareunia and urinary symptoms resulting from oestrogen withdrawal, respond to local applications of oestrogenic creams. Specific treatment should be administered for vaginal infections, if present.</p>
<p>Topical corticosteroids, for example, 0.01% fluocinolone acetonide cream has proved helpful in hypertrophic lesions. A mixture of 1% hydrocortisone and 2 to 3% testosterone three to four times daily has been found to be particularly beneficial in the treatment of lichen sclerosis.</p>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>Warn the patient not to apply an excess of testosterone because it may cause systemic virilising effects in addition to an increase in hair growth.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prognosis">Prognosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the absence of malignancy, the principal goal is to relieve symptoms, which mainly consist of pruritis.</p>
<p>Periodic re-examination is also necessary to detect any malignant changes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="bartholin-s-abscess-or-cyst">Bartholin's Abscess or Cyst<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bartholin-s-abscess-or-cyst" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Can you remember where the Bartholin's gland is situated? See the illustration opposite to help you visualise it.</p>
<p>The most common cause of Bartholin's cyst is a gonococcal infection that causes obstruction. However, another probable cause is congenital narrowing of the duct. The patient will present with:</p>
<ul>
<li>Oedematous and inflamed tissues around the Bartholin's gland</li>
<li>Fluctuant mass, usually palpable</li>
<li>Small non-inflamed cysts are asymptomatic unless progressive enlargement compromises the vaginal introitus or acute infection intervenes</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-501ebd4c.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-bartholin-s-cyst">Treatment of Bartholin's Cyst<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-bartholin-s-cyst" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main treatment for this condition is Incision and Drainage (I&amp;D) of the infected cyst or abscess and preferably marsupialisation, which allows the abscess to drain properly thus preserving the function of the gland. The drained pus should be sent for culture and sensitivity to detect any gonococcal infections.</p>
<p>The patient should be put on appropriate antibiotics.</p>
<p>Do not forget this condition is very painful, which means the patient should also be given analgesics.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260113-fbf7b6a8.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="relaxation-of-pelvic-support">Relaxation of Pelvic Support<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#relaxation-of-pelvic-support" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are three muscles in the pelvic floor known as:</p>
<ul>
<li>The iliococcygeus</li>
<li>The pubococcygeus</li>
<li>The puborectalis</li>
</ul>
<p>In addition, the perineal body is made up of bulbocavernosus muscles and superficial transverse perineal muscles. The two muscles insert into the midline of the perineum, posterior to the vaginal introitus and anterior to the rectum.</p>
<p>The lower rectum and vagina are supported by the bulbocavernosus. The urethra, vagina and rectum are supported by the endopelvic in the middle of the pelvis.</p>
<p>The cardinal ligament and uterosacral ligaments assist in suspending the uterus and adjacent organs so that they do not prolapse whenever there is increase in intra-abdominal pressure.</p>
<p>Excessive stretching and trauma may result in tears of the endopelvic fascia. This allows the base of the bladder to drop posteriorly forming a cystocele. Subsequently the urethra falls away from its normal position behind the symphysis pubis and forms an urethrocele.</p>
<p>The fascial support in the pelvis of Caucasian women seems to be more susceptible to being damaged than that of oriental/black women for reasons that are not yet well understood.</p>
<p>Now move on to look at three conditions that are related to relaxation of the pelvic support. These are cystocele, rectocele, and uterine prolapse.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cystocele">Cystocele<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cystocele" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the herniation of the bladder through the anterior vaginal wall. It may be classified into the following degrees:</p>
<ul>
<li>Mild cystocele, where the anterior vaginal wall prolapses to the introitus upon straining.</li>
<li>Moderate cystocele, where the vaginal wall extends beyond the introitus upon straining.</li>
<li>Severe cystocele, where the vaginal wall extends beyond introitus in the resting state.</li>
</ul>
<p>A small cystocele will generally cause no significant symptoms but if it is a large one, the following symptoms may be noticed:</p>
<ul>
<li>It will bulge out of the vaginal introitus and make the patient complain of vaginal pressure or it may manifest as a</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 258 of 317
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>protruding mass that may give her feeling that she is 'sitting on a ball'.</p>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms are aggravated by vigorous activity, prolonged standing, coughing, sneezing or straining. They are relieved by resting and assuming a recumbent or knee-chest position.</li>
<li>Urinary incontinence or incomplete bladder emptying feeling which may lead to frequent micturition.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-cystocele">Management of Cystocele<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-cystocele" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The management of a patient with this condition will include investigations using urinalysis, x-ray and/or cystoscopy. If the patient is suffering from a small or moderate cystocele, she should be reassured that it is not a serious condition. A woman of childbearing age should not have corrective surgery until she has borne her children. She will need conservative management, which will include:</p>
<ul>
<li>The insertion of a pessary or tampon in the lower part of the vagina, which may provide temporary support. However note that prolonged use may eventually lead to pressure necrosis and vaginal lacerations.</li>
<li>Exercises in young patients will give definite improvement of pressure symptoms.</li>
<li>Oestrogen in post-menopausal women for a number of months may greatly improve the tone, quality and vascularity of musculo-fascial support.</li>
<li>Surgical measures especially for large cystoceles, causing retention and recurrent bladder infection. The most common measure is anterior-vaginal colporrhaphy, which ensures the most effective surgical correction of a cystocele. By preventing further pregnancies, a hysterectomy averts the problem of vaginal delivery, which would destroy the bladder support provided by the anterior colporrhaphy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-cystocele">Prevention of Cystocele<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-cystocele" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A woman should do intrapartum and postpartum exercises, especially those designed to strengthen the levator and perineal muscles groups.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Correct or avoid obesity, chronic coughs, straining and traumatic deliveries.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Oestrogen therapy maintains the musculo-fascial tissue after menopause and prevents or postpones the appearance of cystocele and other forms of pelvic relaxation.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The prognosis for recovery is excellent after surgery in the absence of subsequent deliveries or stress that increases intra-abdominal pressure.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rectocele">Rectocele<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rectocele" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the herniation of the rectum through the posterior vaginal wall. Some of the causes of this condition include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Disruption of the fibrous connective tissue (recto-vaginal fascia) between the rectum and vagina during childbirth.</li>
<li>Operative deliveries, especially of a large foetus or breech delivery.</li>
<li>Slow involutional changes in the pelvic musculo-fascial supporting tissues as a result of menopause.</li>
<li>Bowel habits whereby lifelong chronic constipation with straining at stool causes this condition.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>
<p>Early and adequate episiotomy reduces the amount of damage to the recto-vaginal fascial supporting tissues.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-diagnosis">Clinical Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A small rectocele is usually demonstrable in virtually all multiparous patients and usually causes no symptoms but the following are essentials of diagnosis:</p>
<ul>
<li>Difficult evacuation of faeces.</li>
<li>Sensation of vaginal fullness expressed as 'falling-out' pressure.</li>
<li>Presence of soft, reducible mass bulging into lower half of the posterior vaginal wall, frequently a flat lacerated perineal body.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-rectocele">Management of Rectocele<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-rectocele" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The management of this condition will include digital extraction if there is faecal impaction.
